</th>

</table>
<p>The <b>Netherlands national football team</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl"><i>Het Nederlands Elftal</i></span>) represents the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> in international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. It is controlled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Football_Association" title="Royal Netherlands Football Association">Royal Netherlands Football Association</a> (KNVB), the governing body for <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> in the Netherlands.</p>
<p>The team is colloquially referred to as <i>Het Nederlands Elftal</i> (The Dutch Eleven) and <i>Oranje</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orange-Nassau" title="House of Orange-Nassau">House of Orange-Nassau</a>. Like the country itself, the team is sometimes incorrectly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_(toponymy)" title="Netherlands (toponymy)">(also colloquially) referred to as <b>Holland</b></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Dutch hold the record for playing the most <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals without ever winning the tournament. They finished second in the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1978 FIFA World Cup">1978</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a> World Cups, losing to <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> respectively;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup>although they won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">1988</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Recentism" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Recentism.svg"><img alt="Recentism.svg" data-file-height="230" data-file-width="265" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Recentism.svg/46px-Recentism.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Recentism.svg/69px-Recentism.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Recentism.svg/92px-Recentism.svg.png 2x" width="46"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article or section <b>might be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Recentism" title="Wikipedia:Recentism">slanted towards recent events</a>.</b> <span class="hide-when-compact">Please try to keep recent events in historical perspective.</span> <small><i>(June 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_national_football_team" title="History of the Netherlands national football team">History of the Netherlands national football team</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3590" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/250px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/375px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/500px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Netherlands in 1905</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands played their first international match in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> on 30 April 1905. The players were selected by a five-member commission from the Dutch football association. After 90 minutes, the score was 1–1, but because the match was for a trophy (the "Coupe van den Abeele"), the game went into extra time, in which <a href="/wiki/Eddy_de_Neve" title="Eddy de Neve">Eddy de Neve</a> scored three times, making the score 4–1 for the Dutch side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands made their first appearance at the World Cup final tournament in <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934</a>. After a second appearance in <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938</a> they did not appear in another World Cup until <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_Football_in_the_1970s">Total Football in the 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Total Football in the 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1970s saw the invention of <a href="/wiki/Total_Football" title="Total Football">Total Football</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl"><i>Totaalvoetbal</i></span>), pioneered by <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> and led by playmaker <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a> and national team coach <a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a>. The Dutch made significant strides, qualifying for two World Cup finals in the decade. The captain of the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian</a> team that won the <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alberto_Torres" title="Carlos Alberto Torres">Carlos Alberto</a>, went on to say, "The only team I've seen that did things differently was Holland at <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">the 1974 World Cup in Germany</a>. Since then everything looks more or less the same to me.... Their 'carousel' style of play was amazing to watch and marvellous for the game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1974, the Netherlands beat both Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> in the second group stage, reaching the final for the first time in their history. However, the team lost to <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1974 FIFA World Cup Final">the final</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, despite having gone 1–0 up through <a href="/wiki/Johan_Neeskens" title="Johan Neeskens">Johan Neeskens</a>' early <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> before a German had even touched the ball. However, a converted penalty by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Breitner" title="Paul Breitner">Paul Breitner</a> and the winner from <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a> led to a victory for the Germans.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311,_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM,_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="793" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311,_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM,_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Dutch team before their 1–2 loss against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in the final of the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 World Cup</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By comparison, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1976" title="UEFA Euro 1976">Euro '76</a> was a disappointment. The Netherlands lost in the semi-finals to <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a>, as much because of infighting within the squad and the coach <a href="/wiki/George_Knobel" title="George Knobel">George Knobel</a>, as well as the skill of the eventual winners.</p>
<p>In 1978, the Netherlands again reached the final of a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>, only to be beaten by the hosts, this time Argentina. This side played without <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johan_Cruijff" title="Johan Cruijff">Johan Cruijff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willem_van_Hanegem" title="Willem van Hanegem">Willem van Hanegem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Beveren" title="Jan van Beveren">Jan van Beveren</a>, who refused to participate in the World Cup. It still contained <a href="/wiki/Johan_Neeskens" title="Johan Neeskens">Johan Neeskens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Rep" title="Johnny Rep">Johnny Rep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arie_Haan" title="Arie Haan">Arie Haan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Krol" title="Ruud Krol">Ruud Krol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Jansen" title="Wim Jansen">Wim Jansen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Jongbloed" title="Jan Jongbloed">Jan Jongbloed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Suurbier" title="Wim Suurbier">Wim Suurbier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Rensenbrink" title="Rob Rensenbrink">Rob Rensenbrink</a> from the 1974 selection. The Netherlands were less impressive in the group stages. They qualified as runners-up, after a draw with <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru</a> and a loss to <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a>. In the second group phase, however, the Netherlands topped a group including <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> and West Germany, setting up <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1978 FIFA World Cup Final">a final with Argentina</a>. However, the Dutch finished as runners up for the second World Cup in a row as they ultimately lost 3–1 after two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time" title="Extra time">extra time</a> goals from Argentina. Rensenbrink hit the Argentinian post in the last minute of normal time, with the score 1–1.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Failure:_1982.E2.80.9386">Failure: 1982–86</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Failure: 1982–86">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980" title="UEFA Euro 1980">Euro '80</a> was the last tournament for which the Total Football team qualified, but they did not advance past the group stage, despite the tournament format being expanded that year. Veterans such as Krol and Rensenbrink retired soon afterwards and the Dutch team hit a low point in their history: they missed the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 World Cup</a> in Spain, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">Euro '84</a> in France, and the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a> in Mexico. Qualification for Euro 1984 was within reach, but the Dutch ended the campaign on the same number of points as rivals Spain, and the same goal difference (+16). Spain advanced having scored two more goals. The failure to reach the 1986 World Cup was also very close. In a play off with neighbours Belgium, the Netherlands lost 1–0 in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, but were leading 2–0 in the home leg in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> with a few minutes remaining. Belgium scored to end the tie 2–1, and overall play off 2–2. Belgium advanced on the away goal rule.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_champions">European champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Beker.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/170px-De_Beker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/255px-De_Beker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/340px-De_Beker.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Beker.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 1988 trophy on display in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="849" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg/160px-Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg/240px-Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg/320px-Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rinus_Michels_1984b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a> returned, with his technical assistant Joris van Beek, to coach the team for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">Euro '88</a> tournament in West Germany. After losing the first group match against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR_national_football_team" title="USSR national football team">Soviet Union</a> (1–0), the Netherlands qualified for the semi-final by defeating <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> 3–1 (with a hat-trick by the tournament's top scorer <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> (1–0). For many Dutch football supporters, the most important match in the tournament was the semi-final against West Germany, the host country, considered a revenge for the lost 1974 World Cup final (also in West Germany). Marco van Basten scored in the 89th minute to sink the German side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> The Netherlands won the final with a victory over the USSR through a header by <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a> and a volley by Van Basten. This was the national team's first major tournament win, and it restored them to the forefront of international football for the next three years after almost a decade in the wilderness.</p>
<p>Despite high expectations as the team entered the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 World Cup</a> in Italy, the tournament was not a success, as strife within the squad and managerial instability (<a href="/wiki/Thijs_Libregts" title="Thijs Libregts">Thijs Libregts</a> took over from Michels only to be fired shortly after the team qualified, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Leo_Beenhakker" title="Leo Beenhakker">Leo Beenhakker</a> for the finals) ultimately tore the team apart. Van Basten failed to score, as he was frequently marked by opposing defenders, while Gullit was ineffective having not fully recovered from injury. The Dutch managed to advance despite drawing all three group games, meeting their arch-rivals West Germany in the round of 16. The match is most remembered for the spitting-incident involving <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rudi_V%C3%B6ller" title="Rudi Völler">Rudi Völler</a> as the Netherlands lost 2–1.</p>
<p>The team reached the semi-finals in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">Euro '92</a> in Sweden, which was noted for the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a>, but they were eliminated by eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>, with Van Basten's kick in the penalty shootout being saved by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmeichel" title="Peter Schmeichel">Peter Schmeichel</a>. This was to be Van Basten's last major tournament as he suffered a serious ankle injury shortly after, eventually conceding defeat and retiring at the age of 30 in 1995; it was also the last hurrah for Rinus Michels, who returned for one final spell in charge of the team before retiring for good after the tournament ended.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a> took over from Michels on the understanding that he himself would be replaced by Johan Cruijff the following year, although Advocaat actually stayed in charge for over two years. In the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a> in the United States, in the absence of the injured Van Basten and the <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">striking</a> Gullit, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a> led the team with three goals and the Netherlands advanced to the quarter-finals, where they lost 3–2 to eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contrasting_fortunes:_1996.E2.80.93">Contrasting fortunes: 1996–</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Contrasting fortunes: 1996–">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro '96</a>, after drawing with <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> and beating <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>, the Dutch faced the hosts England in the Group A decider, and lost 4–1, with <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a>'s late consolation enough to finish second on goals scored. They then played <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> in the quarter-finals and lost on penalties.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="800" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/220px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/330px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/440px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Netherlands at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro 96</a> in a match against Scotland at the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a> stadium in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, England.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a>, a Dutch team including <a href="/wiki/Marc_Overmars" title="Marc Overmars">Marc Overmars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Cocu" title="Phillip Cocu">Phillip Cocu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_de_Boer" title="Frank de Boer">Frank de Boer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_de_Boer" title="Ronald de Boer">Ronald de Boer</a> and Kluivert, met Argentina in the quarter-final and won 2–1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> before losing on penalties to <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> and in the third-place play-off to <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>. Soon afterwards, manager <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> resigned to be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>. The Netherlands co-hosted <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> with Belgium and won all three wins in the group stage and then defeated Yugoslavia 6–1 in the quarter-finals. In the semi-finals, Italian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Toldo" title="Francesco Toldo">Francesco Toldo</a> made two penalty shootout saves to eliminate the Netherlands. The Netherlands failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup</a> after crucial losses to <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>, and manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> resigned.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="416" data-file-width="1143" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/325px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/488px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/650px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Netherlands at the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a> returned to coach the Netherlands for a second time. In his first game, a 1–0 win over Spain on 27 March,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the Netherlands won the <a href="/wiki/Unofficial_Football_World_Championships" title="Unofficial Football World Championships">Unofficial Football World Championships</a> (UFWC). In addition, on 21 August, the Netherlands won <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasazzi%27s_Baton" title="Nasazzi's Baton">Nasazzi's Baton</a>, defeating Norway 1–0, unifying for the first time the two trophies. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> He led the team to the semifinals of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> where they lost to the hosts Portugal.</p>
<p>The Netherlands qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> under new manager Marco van Basten and were eliminated in the second round after losing 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>, in a match that produced 16 yellow cards (which matched the World Cup record for most cautions in one game set in 2002) and set a new World Cup record of four red cards (two for either side); it was nicknamed "the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(association_football)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (association football)">Battle of Nuremberg</a>" by the press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> Despite criticism surrounding his selection policy and the lack of attacking football from his team, Van Basten was offered a two-year extension to his contract by the KNVB, which would allow him to serve as national coach during <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> The Netherlands qualified for Euro 2008, where they were drawn in the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Death" title="Group of Death">Group of Death</a>," together with <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> and Romania. They began with a 3–0 win over World champions Italy in <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a>, a first victory over that opponent since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1978_World_Cup" title="1978 World Cup">1978</a>. They lost in the quarter-finals to Hiddink's <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> 3–1, with <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a> scoring an 86th-minute equaliser to force extra time where the Russians went on to score twice.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1523" data-file-width="2523" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/220px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/330px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/440px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Netherlands – France at Euro 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1532" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/220px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/330px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/440px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Netherlands – Denmark at the 2010 World Cup</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under new coach <a href="/wiki/Bert_van_Marwijk" title="Bert van Marwijk">Bert van Marwijk</a>, the Dutch went on to secure a 100 percent record in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_9" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group 9">their World Cup 2010 qualification campaign</a> to qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>. In the quarter-finals against <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>, the Brazilians held a 1–0 lead at the half and had never lost in 37 World Cup matches (35–0–2) in which they had held a half-time lead, but the Dutch scored twice to advance. In the semi-final, the Dutch beat <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> 3–2 to advance to their first World Cup final since 1978, where they would fall to <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> 1–0 after midfielder <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Iniesta" title="Andrés Iniesta">Andrés Iniesta</a> scored in extra time. From August to September 2011, the team was ranked number one in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>, thus becoming the second national football team, after Spain, to top the rankings without previously winning a World Cup. For <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, the Netherlands were placed in Group B alongside with <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>, dubbed the tournament's "Group of Death." The Netherlands lost all three of its matches. Johan Cruyff criticised the team's star players of poor build up play and sloppy execution of the easy passes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> while manager <a href="/wiki/Bert_van_Marwijk" title="Bert van Marwijk">Bert van Marwijk</a> resigned after the disappointment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louis van Gaal then became manager for the second time. In the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 World Cup UEFA qualifying round</a>, the Netherlands won nine games and drew one, topping the group and earning automatic qualification. They were drawn into <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B" title="2014 FIFA World Cup Group B">Group B</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>. The team avenged their <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2010 FIFA World Cup Final">2010 defeat</a> by defeating title holders Spain 5–1 in their opening match, with <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> scoring two goals each, and <a href="/wiki/Stefan_de_Vrij" title="Stefan de Vrij">Stefan de Vrij</a> the other. After the Dutch fell behind 1–0 from conceding a penalty, Van Persie equalized just before half time with an acrobatic diving header that gave him the nickname "The Flying Dutchman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_FIFIA_World_Cup,_Semi_final,_NED-ARG(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="960" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/220px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/330px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/440px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_FIFIA_World_Cup,_Semi_final,_NED-ARG(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Dutch team leaves the field after losing to Argentina</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands defeated <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> 2–1 in the round of 16, with <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a> equalising late in the match, and <a href="/wiki/Klaas-Jan_Huntelaar" title="Klaas-Jan Huntelaar">Klaas-Jan Huntelaar</a> scoring a controversial penalty after a foul on <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> in stoppage time. In the quarter-finals, where they faced <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a>, the Dutch had many shots on goal but could not score, with the match finishing in a 0–0 draw after extra time. The Netherlands won the ensuing penalty shootout 4–3 in large part due to backup goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Tim_Krul" title="Tim Krul">Tim Krul</a>, who was brought on just before the end of extra time and made two saves, marking the first time in World Cup history a goalkeeper was brought onto the field solely to participate in a shootout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> In the semi-final game against Argentina, the Netherlands had a good chance to score from Arjen Robben while managing to contain <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a>, and both teams finished scoreless after extra time. In penalty kicks, however, the Dutch were eliminated 4–2, with <a href="/wiki/Ron_Vlaar" title="Ron Vlaar">Ron Vlaar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a> having their spot kicks saved by <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Romero" title="Sergio Romero">Sergio Romero</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The Netherlands won the third-place match against the hosts. Van Gaal, who successfully motivated the team after their semi-final knockout,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> received praise for getting more out of the young and inexperienced Netherlands squad than many expected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> He left to become manager of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.</p>
<p>Van Gaal was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">Euro 2016 qualifying</a> campaign. On 29 June 2015 Hiddink left his position as manager, and was succeeded by assistant Blind. The Netherlands came fourth in their group, failing to qualify for the European Championship for the first time since <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">1984</a> and a major tournament for the first time since the 2002 World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_image">Team image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Team image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours">Colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1668" data-file-width="3012" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/220px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/330px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/440px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dutch fans wearing the <a href="/wiki/Oranjegekte" title="Oranjegekte">traditional orange</a> colours at a <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> match in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands national football team famously plays in bright orange shirts. Orange is the historic <a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">national colour</a> of the Netherlands, originating from one of the many titles of the ruling head of state, <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Orange" title="Prince of Orange">Prince of Orange</a>, which is also the color of the same name. The current Dutch away shirt is blue.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Kit_(association_football)" title="Kit (association football)">kit</a> provider to the national team, a sponsorship that began in 1996 and is contracted to continue until at least 2026.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93Netherlands_football_rivalry" title="Germany–Netherlands football rivalry">Germany–Netherlands football rivalry</a></div>
<p>Netherlands' long-time football rival is <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>. The rivalry is one of the few long-standing football rivalries at a national level. Beginning in 1974, when the Dutch lost the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a> to West Germany in the final (though deeply rooted in Dutch <a href="/wiki/Anti-German_sentiment" title="Anti-German sentiment">anti-German sentiment</a> due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="History of the Netherlands (1939–1945)">occupation of the Netherlands by Germany</a> during World War II), the rivalry between the two nations has become one of the best-known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_association_football_club_rivalries_by_country" title="List of association football club rivalries by country">international football rivalries</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Low Countries derby</a></div>
<p>To a minor extent, the Netherlands maintains a rivalry with their other neighbours, <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a>; a Belgian-Dutch (football) duel is referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Low Countries derby</a>. More recently, the Netherlands have also developed a rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espnfc_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-espnfc-29">[28]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_and_fixtures">Results and fixtures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Results and fixtures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><i>For all past match results of the national team, see the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team_results" title="Netherlands national football team results">team's results page</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>The following matches were played or are scheduled to be played by the national team in the current or upcoming seasons. The time in the Netherlands is shown first. If the local time is different, it will be displayed below.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Tournaments">Other Tournaments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other Tournaments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team#Belgium_vs._Netherlands_Cups" title="Belgium national football team">Coupe Vanden Abeele</a></b>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners:</b> 1905, 1907, 1908, 1909, 1911, 1912, 1914</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team#Belgium_vs._Netherlands_Cups" title="Belgium national football team">Rotterdamsch Nieuwsblad Cup</a></b>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners:</b> 1905, 1908, 1909, 1910, 1911, 1912, 1914</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1928_Summer_Olympics#Consolation_first_round" title="Football at the 1928 Summer Olympics">Olympic Football Consolation Tournament</a></b>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners:</b> <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1928_Summer_Olympics#Consolation_final" title="Football at the 1928 Summer Olympics">1928</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Challenge" title="Nelson Mandela Challenge">Nelson Mandela Inauguration Challenge Cup</a></b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners:</b> <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team_1997#South_Africa_vs_Netherlands" title="Netherlands national football team 1997">1997</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_national_football_team#FIFA_75th_Anniversary_Cup" title="History of the Netherlands national football team">75th Anniversary FIFA Cup</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Runners-up: 1979</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1980_Mundialito" title="1980 Mundialito">World Champions' Gold Cup</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Fourth Place: <a href="/wiki/1980_Mundialito#Final_ranking" title="1980 Mundialito">1980</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_in_Uruguayan_football#Copa_Confraternidad_de_Antel" title="2010–11 in Uruguayan football">Copa Confraternidad</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Runners-up: 2011</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A2ton_de_Nasazzi" title="fr:Bâton de Nasazzi">Nasazzi's Baton</a></b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners:</b> 1978, 1985, 1998, 2000, 2002, 2008</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that this match is not considered to be a full international by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Football_Association" title="English Football Association">English Football Association</a>, and does not appear in the records of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England team</a>, because professional football had already been introduced in England at that time. In the Netherlands however, professional football would only be introduced in 1954, and before that time, players who left the Netherlands to turn pro in another country were banned from the national team.</span></li>
